  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }

Ever since that terrible night two years ago when his mother told him to run, he has lived alone on the streets of Boston, surviving by his wits, staying one step ahead of the police and the truant officers.<br/><br/>One day, Magnus learns that someone else is trying to track him down—his uncle Randolph, a man his mother had always warned </span>
  <span id="freeText7686791358232473411" style="display:none">Magnus Chase has seen his share of trouble. Ever since that terrible night two years ago when his mother told him to run, he has lived alone on the streets of Boston, surviving by his wits, staying one step ahead of the police and the truant officers.<br /><br />One day, Magnus learns that someone else is trying to track him down—his uncle Randolph, a man his mother had always warned him about. When Magnus tries to outmaneuver his uncle, he falls right into his clutches. Randolph starts rambling about Norse history and Magnus's birthright: a weapon that has been lost for thousands of years.<br /><br />The more Randolph talks, the more puzzle pieces fall into place. Stories about the gods of Asgard, wolves, and Doomsday bubble up from Magnus's memory. But he doesn't have time to consider it all before a fire giant attacks the city, forcing him to choose between his own safety and the lives of hundreds of innocents. . . .<br /><br />Sometimes, the only way to start a new life is to die.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It is her cousin, because in the Blood of Olympus Annabeth said that she had an uncle and cousin from Boston that she wished she knew better, and thei<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It is her cousin, because in the Blood of Olympus Annabeth said that she had an uncle and cousin from Boston that she wished she knew better, and their last name just happened to be Chase. I would personally be shocked if this wasn't foreshadowing for this next series. Fingers crossed that they somehow come together a little bit, and even if Annabeth is not in it, we get to hear more about her and Percy, and the rest of the 7.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Norse Mythology is pretty big on suffering (Odin hung himself for nine days and nights as a sacrifice, pierced by his own spear) and death/reincarnati<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Norse Mythology is pretty big on suffering (Odin hung himself for nine days and nights as a sacrifice, pierced by his own spear) and death/reincarnation (Gullveig was burnt three times, three times reborn). As well all of Odin's warriors/kings in Valhalla were slain ( the einherjar chosen by Valkyries).<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>    </div>
</div>

<div id="review_1422129551" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1422129551" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1422129551?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=paranormal-uf">paranormal-uf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1422129551" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15545619928255088767">2 1/2 stars.<br/><br/>Middle grade it may be, but I really enjoyed <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28187.The_Lightning_Thief__Percy_Jackson_and_the_Olympians___1_' title='The Lightning Thief (Percy Jackson and the Olympians, #1) by Rick Riordan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Lightning Thief</a>. I thought it was creative, fast-paced, entertaining and with a great message for all kids who feel a little on the outside sometimes. As with Harry Potter, it takes a normal, seemingly unremarkable kid and propels him into a world where he's a hero. And it's just fun!<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15724396.The_Sword_of_Summer__Magnus_Chase_and_the_Gods_of_Asgard___1_' title='The Sword of Summer (Magnus Chase and the Gods of Asgard, #1) by Rick Riordan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Sword of Summer</a>, though, doesn't feel... like anything new. Some people will shriek "No!" at this, but I really think it's time for Mr Riordan to move</span>
  <span id="freeText15545619928255088767" style="display:none">2 1/2 stars.<br /><br />Middle grade it may be, but I really enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28187.The_Lightning_Thief__Percy_Jackson_and_the_Olympians___1_" title="The Lightning Thief (Percy Jackson and the Olympians, #1) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lightning Thief</a>. I thought it was creative, fast-paced, entertaining and with a great message for all kids who feel a little on the outside sometimes. As with Harry Potter, it takes a normal, seemingly unremarkable kid and propels him into a world where he's a hero. And it's just fun!<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15724396.The_Sword_of_Summer__Magnus_Chase_and_the_Gods_of_Asgard___1_" title="The Sword of Summer (Magnus Chase and the Gods of Asgard, #1) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sword of Summer</a>, though, doesn't feel... like anything new. Some people will shriek "No!" at this, but I really think it's time for Mr Riordan to move on from these stories about young heroes and heroines and Greek/Roman/Egyptian/Norse Gods. At this point, the stories are all starting to blend into one and it feels like his well of ideas has run dry.<br /><br /><b>It's incredibly hard to distinguish Magnus's voice from that of Percy Jackson</b>. It's pretty much the same kid again, with the same wit and snark, he's just been given a different name. Instead of being the son of a Greek god, though, Magnus is the son of a Norse god - a difference that doesn't make the story different enough, but does provide some major info-dumpy moments.<br /><br />Don't get me wrong, Riordan's writing is still easy to read and quite funny. Magnus makes lots of snarky comments to ensure that the book never becomes too serious. But is it enough? Sadly, I don't think so.<br /><br />I guess Riordan has a tried and tested formula that he applies to all his books, but it's starting to show. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15724396.The_Sword_of_Summer__Magnus_Chase_and_the_Gods_of_Asgard___1_" title="The Sword of Summer (Magnus Chase and the Gods of Asgard, #1) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sword of Summer</a> was predictable and none of the characters really stood out - I honestly doubt I will remember their names in a few days time.<br /><br />As much as it will hurt the author's loyal fans, there comes a time when every author must move onto something new. For Riordan, I think it should be now.<br /><br /><b>ALSO:</b> Completely unrelated to the book's content, but that guy on the cover does not look a teenager. In fact, he looks just like Kurt Cobain.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/bookgeekreviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15545619928255088767" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16762753271191571602">I finally read this book, after my pre-review got so disturbingly popular. I'm not impressed. It was amusing, but I didn't particularly care about the characters, and I was bored through most of its 500 pages. <br/><br/>Maybe the Percy Jackson concept is something that only works once, and now it's just being overused. It doesn't help that this book is full of Percy Jackson references that seem, well, masturbatory. And pop culture references that will look dated in less than 5 years. <br/><br/>Count me out for the </span>
  <span id="freeText16762753271191571602" style="display:none">I finally read this book, after my pre-review got so disturbingly popular. I'm not impressed. It was amusing, but I didn't particularly care about the characters, and I was bored through most of its 500 pages. <br><br>Maybe the Percy Jackson concept is something that only works once, and now it's just being overused. It doesn't help that this book is full of Percy Jackson references that seem, well, masturbatory. And pop culture references that will look dated in less than 5 years. <br><br>Count me out for the rest of the series.<br><br><b>Pre-review: </b>I've heard rumors about a Norse mythology book by Riordan, but only now has it popped up on Goodreads. I'm super excited! It better be as good as Percy Jackson. <br><br>I hope it has some of this: <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403671ra/785382.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Actually, I hope this series is better than Percy Jackson, because this time, Riordan has the opportunity to put Loki in it.<br><span>[image error]</span><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403671ra/785384.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br>Yep, I'm having a good time here. Though I don't know why that would ever happen, but I can always hope.<br><span>[image error]</span><br><br>In all seriousness, there's some complex emotional stuff going on with Loki and Riordan will be missing a golden opportunity if he doesn't take advantage of it.<br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403671ra/785392.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>(Yep, this review keeps getting bigger and bigger.)<br><br>I leave you with this GIF of Loki. <div id="review_1067355764" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Darth J " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18974711-darth-j"><img alt="Darth J " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456429148p2/18974711.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1067355764?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Darth J " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Darth J " href="/user/show/18974711-darth-j">Darth J </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18974711-darth-j?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1067355764" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8922767258365535708"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444746757ra/16547166.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>I'll give Riordan credit for his mythological research, but his writing and characterizations need a lot of work still. Not only does <b>Magnus have the exact same voice and personality as Percy Jackson and Jason Grace</b>, but they all have a weird combination of forced snark and dad jokes that makes them sound more cartoonish than believable--and you need something to ground characters in reality when you have all this magical stuff happening. While it's great that he's trying to include more diversi</span>
  <span id="freeText8922767258365535708" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444746757ra/16547166.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I'll give Riordan credit for his mythological research, but his writing and characterizations need a lot of work still. Not only does <b>Magnus have the exact same voice and personality as Percy Jackson and Jason Grace</b>, but they all have a weird combination of forced snark and dad jokes that makes them sound more cartoonish than believable--and you need something to ground characters in reality when you have all this magical stuff happening. While it's great that he's trying to include more diversity with his cast, the fact that the <i>Muslim girl has a shape-shifting hijab</i> seems just as ham-fisted and clueless as when he degraded Nico into a stereotype in the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/733467542?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>last book</b>
</a>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444748532i/16547354._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Wait, is this a hint at Riordan's <i>Da Vinci Code</i>-inspired mashup with Dan Brown?! In all seriousness, we do have a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1410727890?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>new series</b>
</a> coming our way and the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1410730448?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>next book</b>
</a> has been announced as well.<br><br>Those looking for more of a connection to previous books than just Annabeth Chase showing up will be disappointed, as it doesn't seem like this series will interconnect the same way that <i>Heroes of Olympus</i> did with <i>Percy Jackson and the Olympians</i>.<br><br>Also, I'm taking off a point for this:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444748199i/16547302._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>(Ask the fandom community if you don't already know)</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444749260ra/16547422.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="8922767258365535708" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2190394857" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2190394857" />
    <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin"><img alt="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603831478p2/17438949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2190394857?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin">Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=fantasy-all">fantasy-all</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2190394857" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10845528329303490925"><b>UPDATE: First 3 books are 99 cents on Kindle US 5/19/19</b><br/><br/>I enjoyed this book a great deal. I'm wanting to get into more Norse Mythology and even though this was a more funny take on those things I still enjoyed it. One star off for making my wolves the bad guys in a book once again. < -- And no, I need no commentary on that. <br/><br/>I loved Magnus friends, well I loved him too. There is a lot of snark and funny moments in the book. And I figured that going into this. I WILL be reading as many books as I c</span>
  <span id="freeText10845528329303490925" style="display:none"><b>UPDATE: First 3 books are 99 cents on Kindle US 5/19/19</b><br /><br />I enjoyed this book a great deal. I'm wanting to get into more Norse Mythology and even though this was a more funny take on those things I still enjoyed it. One star off for making my wolves the bad guys in a book once again. &lt; -- And no, I need no commentary on that. <br /><br />I loved Magnus friends, well I loved him too. There is a lot of snark and funny moments in the book. And I figured that going into this. I WILL be reading as many books as I can of Vikings etc that are more history based. <br /><br />Magnus has no idea who his father is as it goes and he has to hunt for a sword so the world doesn't come to an end. Well, that is something to lay on a kid who has been living on the streets for two years. He has some trusty friends named, Hearth and Blitzen, that stay with him. They turn out to be something else and I love them to pieces. <br /><br />There are other friends in the book that I enjoyed: <br />Sam<br />X<br />Mallory<br />TJ<br />Halfborn Gunderson<br /><br />and I probably left someone out as I tend to do, but not on purpose. <br /><br />I will continue on with the series to see what they get up to in their next adventures. <br /><br />I will leave you will a couple of excerpts. <br /><br /><b>
  <blockquote>I'd seen some weird stuff in my life. <br /><br />I once watched a crowd of people wearing nothing but Speedos and Santa hats job down Boylston in the middle of winter. I met a guy who could play the harmonica with his nose, a drum set with his feet, a guitar with his hands, and a xylophone with his butt all at the same time. I knew a woman who'd adopted a grocery cart and named it Clarence. Then there was this dude who claimed to be from Alpha Centauri and had philosophical conversations with Canadian geese. <br /><br />**<br /><br />"Long enough to know you're an idiot," she grumbled.<br />"What she's trying to say," T.J. offered, "is that hallmates always protect each other. We'll cover your escape."<br /><br />The door of my room shook, Cracks spiderwebbed from the nameplate. A decorative spear off the way of the corridor. <br /><br />"X!" T.J. called. "Help!"<br /><br />The half-troll's door expolded off its hinges. X lumbered into the hallway as if he'd been standing just inside, waiting for the call. "Yes?"<br /><br />T.J pointed. "Magnus's door. Squirrel."<br />"Okay."<br /><br />X marched over and shoved his back against my door. It shuddered again, but X held firm. Enraged barking echoed from inside. <br /><br />Halfborn Gunderson stumbled out of his room wearing nothing but smiley-face boxers, double-bladed axes in his hands. <br /><br />"What's going on?" He glowered at Blitz and Hearth. <br />"Should I kill the dwarf and the elf?"<br /><br />"No!" Blitzen yelped. "Don't kill the dwarf and the elf!" <br />"They're with me," I said. "We're leaving."<br />"Squirrel," T.J. explained <br /><br />Halfborn's shaggy eyebrows achieved orbit. "Squirrel as in squirrel, squirrel?"<br />"Squirrel squirrel," Mallory agreed. "And I'm surrounded by morons morons."<br /><br />A raven soared down the hall. It landed on the nearest light fixture and squawked at me accusingly.<br /><br />"Well, that's great," Mallory said. "The ravens have sensed your friends' intrusion. That means the Valkyries won't be far behind."</blockquote>
</b><br /><br />Happy Reading! <br /><br />Mel ♥<br /><br />MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2018/01/the-sword-of-summer-by-rick-riordan.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10845528329303490925" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer17120627470202713521">See more reviews at <a href='http://yamidnightreads.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>YA Midnight Reads</a><br/><br/>THE SWORD OF SUMMER was released today! Whoop xD GET YOUR BUTTS MOVING PEOPLE AND GO BUY A COPY FROM YOUR LOCAL BOOKSTORE TODAY :D<br/><br/><strong>*This review is spoiler-free*<br/><br/>4.5 stars</strong><br/><br/>Rick Riordan’s books were some of the first novels I read as a reader, and throughout these past years, <strong>his books have always remained my all time favourites</strong>. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28187.The_Lightning_Thief' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Percy Jackson</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7736182-the-lost-hero' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Heroes of Olympus</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7090447-the-red-pyramid' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kane Chronicles</a>, and now you can add <em>Magnus Chase</em> to that list of awesome. Why? BECAUSE <em>THE SWORD OF S</em></span>
  <span id="freeText17120627470202713521" style="display:none">See more reviews at <a href="http://yamidnightreads.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">YA Midnight Reads</a><br><br>THE SWORD OF SUMMER was released today! Whoop xD GET YOUR BUTTS MOVING PEOPLE AND GO BUY A COPY FROM YOUR LOCAL BOOKSTORE TODAY :D<br><br><strong>*This review is spoiler-free*<br><br>4.5 stars</strong><br><br>Rick Riordan’s books were some of the first novels I read as a reader, and throughout these past years, <strong>his books have always remained my all time favourites</strong>. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28187.The_Lightning_Thief" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Percy Jackson</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7736182-the-lost-hero" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Heroes of Olympus</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7090447-the-red-pyramid" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Kane Chronicles</a>, and now you can add <em>Magnus Chase</em> to that list of awesome. Why? BECAUSE <em>THE SWORD OF SUMMER</em> WAS FANTABULOUS.<br><br>In fact, I loved this book so much that I bookmarked all the funny bits + my favourite parts… which was <strong>basically the whole book</strong>. <em>Whoops</em>.<br><br><a href="http://yamidnightreads.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/10/15706896.png" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443840049i/16419080.png" alt="Bookmarks The Sword of Summer" width="400" height="533" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Just a note: <em>The Sword of Summer</em> is <strong>perfectly readable and spoiler free if you have not read any <em>Percy Jackson</em> book</strong>. But, it would certainly add to the enjoyment of the novel if you did because in usual Riordan style, there’s some inside jokes here and there.<br><br>CAN WE TALK ABOUT HOW WE GET <strong>ANNABETH CAMEOS</strong>?!?!? She doesn’t have a role in the main plotline of the story but she’s there and as fabulous as she is and I totally flailed each time she popped up.<br><br><strong>The <em>Percy Jackson</em> and <em>Magnus Chase</em> books do have parallels and similarities</strong>, but it didn’t feel like I was just reading the same book with different names. While both books have gods and goddesses and demigods and monsters and badass characters and truck loads of humour… yet the characters themselves were all very much unique as well as the plotline and world building etc.<br><br>Talking about Riordan’s out-of-this-world sense of humour, can we just admire it for a while?<br><blockquote>“Could you do a glamour and turn into something smaller?” I asked it. “Preferably not a chain, since it’s no longer the 1990s?”<br>The sword didn’t reply (duh), but I imagined it was humming at a more interrogative pitch, like, <em>Such as what?</em><br>“I dunno. Something pocket-size and innocuous. A pen, maybe?<br>The sword pulsed, almost like it was laughing. I imagined it saying, <em>A pen sword. That is the stupidest thing I’ve ever heard.</em>
</blockquote><br>EXCUST ME MY HEART JUST STOPPED. RICK RIORDAN, YOU ARE SNEAAAAAKY.<br><blockquote>“This is an important battle – the fire lord Surt, Fenris Wolf. Surely that’s worthy of your attention.”<br>Thor’s right eye twitched. “That’s a fine offer. Really. I’d love to, but I have another pressing appointment – ”<br>“<em>Game of Thrones</em>,” Marvin explained.<br>“Shut up!”</blockquote><br>And let’s not forget chapter titles like this: “<em>The Man with the Metal Bra</em>”, “<em>You Had One Job</em>”, “<em>Hearthstone Passes Out Even More than Jason Grace (Though I Have No Idea Who That Is)</em>” (!!!!!) and “<em>How to Kill Giants Politely</em>”.<br><br>Other than his funny dialogue, one of the strongest aspects of <em>The Sword of Summer</em> is in its <strong>diverse set of characters</strong>. Samirah al-Abbas, who is Magnus’ Valkyrie, is a young Muslim girl and wears a hijab. She’s in an arranged marriage that she’s happy is happening (she’s in <em>luuuuurve</em>) and has big dreams for her future. There’s also Blitz (a dwarf) and Hearth (an elf, who also happens to be deaf), and they just bring another level of hilarity to the novel. They pretend to be homeless dudes when they were undercover, looking after Magnus before he was introduced to the whole world of Vikings and monsters and magic.<br><br>I will say there is<strong> ZERO romance</strong> in this book, which I did quite like because dammit, not EVERY romance just happens to begin at the start of a series. Thanks for keeping it realistic, Riordan. I do hope there is a romance in the future books, and I can sorta see one (but maybe that’s my crazy fangirl mind speaking) – we shall see!<br><br><a href="http://yamidnightreads.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/10/Screen-Shot-2015-10-03-at-11.04.13-am.png" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443840049i/16419081._SX540_.png" alt="The Sword of Summer Percy Jackson" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><strong>So why not a full 5 stars?</strong><br><br><strong>1.</strong> I feel like Magnus character could use some more brushing up and development. I love his goofy snarkiness, but feel as if I don’t know him all that well other than his funny side of his personality.<br><br><strong>2.</strong> I feel like the last 1/4 to 1/5 was less enjoyable than rest of the book. I felt a little bored, and you can even tell from my bookmarks because there is less in that area.<br><br>BUT that being said, <strong><em>The Sword of Summer</em> lived up to my expectations and I loved this book through and through.</strong> Diverse and lovable characters, complex world-building, hilarious dialogue (in usual Riordan fashion)… hands down one of my favourite books of 2015. BRING ON BOOK 2.<br><br>----<br><br><b>Edit: 31/07/15</b><br><br>GUYS. LOOK. WHAT. I. HAVE. GOODBYE INTERNET. SEE YOU IN A FEW HOURS.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438350924i/15696351._SX540_.png" width="300" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Edit: 09/10/14</b><br><br>GUYS WE HAVE A SYNOPSIS:<br><br>Magnus Chase has always been a troubled kid. Since his mother's mysterious death, he's lived alone on the streets of Boston, surviving by his wits, keeping one step ahead of the police and the truant officers. One day, he's tracked down by an uncle he's never met—a man his mother claimed was dangerous. His uncle tells him an impossible secret: Magnus is the son of a Norse god. The Viking myths are true. The gods of Asgard are preparing for war. Trolls, giants and worse monsters are stirring for doomsday. To prevent Ragnarok, Magnus must search the Nine Worlds for a weapon that has been lost for thousands of years. When an attack by fire giants forces him to choose between his own safety and the lives of hundreds of innocents, Magnus makes a fatal decision. Sometimes, the only way to start a new life is to die...<br><br>SO MUCH EXCITEMENT. SO IT WAS THE COUSIN. <br><br><br><b>Edit: 07/10/14</b><br><br>My thoughts: Magnus needs to be some close relative of Annabeth's. I highly doubt he'd make Magnus Annabeth and Percy's son, because that would be TOTALLY weird seeing Percabeth all grown up and I'd honestly hate that. So no, let's hope that doesn't happen. <br><br>We can't forget Annabeth has step-brothers...However, <b>SPOILER FOR THE BLOOD OF OLYMPUS:</b> In the book, Annabeth mentions she has an uncle and cousin in Boston but she doesn't really know them because her dad and uncle don't get along well. WAIT WHAT NOW. The only reason I can see for Rick Riordan to include that is to give us a little hint towards who this Magnus Chase guy is.<b>END SPOILER</b><br><br>But regardless, there will have to be Percabeth cameos, right? THERE HAS TO BE. THERE MUST. *nods quickly*<br><br><b>Edit: 07/10/14</b><br><br>MAGNUS CHASE. AS IN ANNABETH CHASE. *screams*<br><br>More info: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://rickriordan.blogspot.com/2014/09/magnus-chase.html">http://rickriordan.blogspot.com/2014/...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17120627470202713521" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2378666796" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2378666796" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2378666796?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" " href="/book/show/28250730-the-sword-of-summer">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2378666796" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8497545680679387867"><i>”The thing about fate, Magnus: even if we can’t change the big picture, our choices can alter the details. That’s how we rebel against destiny, how we make our mark.”</i><br/><br/>And to rebel is exactly what he does! *lol* <br/><br/>Gosh, I really enjoyed this book. It was such a fun read and I once again was hooked from the very first page. Uncle Rick certainly knows how to tell a good story and my heart instantly flew out to Magnus. That poor boy definitely had a hard life and at the beginning of the book I just wan</span>
  <span id="freeText8497545680679387867" style="display:none"><i>”The thing about fate, Magnus: even if we can’t change the big picture, our choices can alter the details. That’s how we rebel against destiny, how we make our mark.”</i><br /><br />And to rebel is exactly what he does! *lol* <br /><br />Gosh, I really enjoyed this book. It was such a fun read and I once again was hooked from the very first page. Uncle Rick certainly knows how to tell a good story and my heart instantly flew out to Magnus. That poor boy definitely had a hard life and at the beginning of the book I just wanted to hug him and give him a home. <br />I mean his mother died, he’s been living on the streets of Boston for two years and now a huge Fire Giant is after him. What a way to start your day. <b>*shakes head*</b><br /><br />And people like me think it’s tough to cook, to do the laundry and to raise your almost two year old rascal who’s in the middle of early terrible twos. XD I’m sure Magnus would switch places in a heartbeat, but then again he probably never experienced the tantrum of a little child. *LOL*<br /><br />Anyway, let’s get back to the book. ;-P<br />What I wanted to say is that I loved Magnus. He’s such an awesome character! He’s funny, he’s intelligent, his heart is at the right place and he knows that <i>“Chocolate must be savoured, not rushed.”</i> How could you not love such a boy? &lt;333<br /><br />Well, of course I liked all of his friends as well. Blitzen and Hearthstone were two really interesting characters and Sam was just kick-ass! XD Plus I loved the way Uncle Rick managed to involve Norse mythology throughout the entire book. It was fun to read all those interesting background stories and I absolutely adored the way he included Boston into his story. =))<br /><br />It’s such a beautiful city and *LOL* the idea of <b>“The World Tree”</b>!!! Boy, I laughed so much! Everyone who ever visited Boston knows about those bronze ducks. It’s just hilarious! Well done Ricky, well done! ;-)<br /><br />The secret star of the entire show and one of my three favourites is <b>“Sumarbrander”</b> though! That sword is soo much fun!!! I can’t wait to read more about him and I really hope he’ll talk even more in the next book! &lt;3<br /><br /><i>”Dude,” said the sword, “I was forged ready.”</i><br /><br /><i>”And another thing!” he yelled. “Giving me away so you could marry a giantess? Dude, what was that? Blades before babes, you know what I’m saying?”</i><br /><br />Jack knows <b>“The Bro Code”</b>!!! Who would have thought it?! *LOL* <br /><br />And this finally brings me to my third favourite person of the book: <b>
  <u>Loki!</u>
</b><br /><br />I’ve always been a huge Loki fan and I was so happy that he was playing a part in this book! (Then again, no surprise there! Everyone who knows a fine share about Norse Mythology also knows that Loki is a constant part of it. As is Thor, but we won’t talk about the blonde Thunder god here. ;-P)<br />I think Loki was portrayed pretty well in this book and his fickle and cunning nature was spot-on. XD<br />I won’t say anything about his role in this book though, I guess you’ll just have to read it if you truly want to find out. (Yes, I’m mean, I know. *lol*)<br /><br />So this said I really enjoyed <b>“The Sword of Summer”</b>! Despite its 489 pages it was actually a very quick read and I can recommend it to everyone. If you love funny adventure stories that are combined with a good dose of mythology this is definitely the right book for you! ;-)</span>
  <a data-text-id="8497545680679387867" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1161565874" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer4312679884067909863"><b>Update 03/28/2020</b>: I really want to get into reading Rick Riordan again. Is The Trials of Apollo any good?<br/><br/>--<br/><br/><b>10/09/2015</b><br/><br/>Guess who's a very grumpy camper? *points to self*<br/><br/>In my own little world, I've always told myself that Rick Riordan can do no wrong. Okay, fine, I sort of hated<em> The Blood of Olympus</em>, but <em>The Sword of Summer</em> was supposed to be a fresh start--<strong>it was supposed to be the book that would put Riordan back up on my mental pedestal</strong>.<br/><br/>Well, I've been fucking let down, Rick. I'm sorry (and sa</span>
  <span id="freeText4312679884067909863" style="display:none"><b>Update 03/28/2020</b>: I really want to get into reading Rick Riordan again. Is The Trials of Apollo any good?<br /><br />--<br /><br /><b>10/09/2015</b><br /><br />Guess who's a very grumpy camper? *points to self*<br /><br />In my own little world, I've always told myself that Rick Riordan can do no wrong. Okay, fine, I sort of hated<em> The Blood of Olympus</em>, but <em>The Sword of Summer</em> was supposed to be a fresh start--<strong>it was supposed to be the book that would put Riordan back up on my mental pedestal</strong>.<br /><br />Well, I've been fucking let down, Rick. I'm sorry (and sad) to have said that, but<em> it's true</em>.<strong> This book </strong>was<strong> just nowhere <em>near</em> the level of </strong>epicness<strong> I was expecting</strong>. Maybe it's because, after ten (eleven if you count <em>Greek Gods</em>) books of kick-butt Greek and Roman mythology, maybe I was just expecting too much.<br /><br />The main thing that made it unenjoyable, at least for me, was its similarity to the original Percy Jackson and the Olympians books, maybe with a little bit of Harry Potter mixed in as well. Let's break it down, shall we?<br /><br /><blockquote>"I did not want to be the harbinger of the wolf. I wanted to be the harbinger of ice cream, or falafel."</blockquote><br /><br />1.) <strong>Magnus's voice sounded exactly like Percy's</strong>. I mean, if you asked me to guess which lines were whose, I wouldn't be able to answer. I might've been okay with it if the sarcastic humor worked with the story, but somehow it didn't. <strong>There was just something a bit more... </strong>juvenile<strong> about the writing style, and it worked with 12 year-old Percy, but not 100% with 16 year-old Magnus</strong>.<br /><br />2.) <strong>All the other characters were just so predictable</strong>. As with PJO, in <em>The Sword of Summer</em>, we're given a hot-headed female who's clearly the most mature in the group, some really quirky sidekick<em>s</em> and sassy villain<em>s</em>. Notice that I said sidekicks and villains as plural nouns--that's because there're more than one of each, and<strong> they all have the same psyche</strong>.<br /><br />3.) <strong>The plot was your typical Rick Riordan storyline</strong>. See, other than his mid-series cliffhangers, <strong>Rick's </strong>books mostly<strong> do just follow a formula plot.</strong> It hurts me to admit that, but yes, it does seem to be the case. You can practically guess the ending without even <em>starting</em> the book.<br /><br />4.) The mythology twists? <strong>I call bullshit at the word "twists"</strong>--I wasn't surprised at all. We've got really obvious villains, which sucks because they were actually unexpected in the original PJO series. But with this? It's basically spoon-fed to us. SPOON-FED.<br /><br />5.) <strong>This book felt <em>horribly</em> info-dumpy</strong>. I NEVER FELT THIS WAY ABOUT THE ORIGINAL PJO SERIES. I'm not even sure why I felt that way with this book... Maybe it's because most of the <strong>Norse mythology facts were just inserted (forcefully) into awkward dialogues in huge chunks</strong>, and I honestly had trouble following along. I CAN'T REMEMBER A THING, AND IT'S ONLY BEEN A DAY.<br /><br />Phew. So glad I finally got that off my chest. Anyway, despite my ranting, this book wasn't horrible--<strong>there were still some quotes that made me chuckle</strong> (especially those lovely chapter headings that we all know and love), parts<strong> that made me immensely sad, and parts that made me root for the main characters. </strong>And, as usual, <strong>Rick's books are just so easy to read.</strong><br /><br />Oh, and <strong>bonus points for diversity</strong>! We have a Muslim demigod as our main heroine (I still don't understand how she's both a Muslim yet a server of the Norse gods), as well as an adorable deaf elf as one of Magnus's sidekicks.<br /><br />And with this, I conclude that I did <em>not</em> love The Sword of Summer, but am hoping for a 200% energy boost for the sequel when it comes out. Please make it ten times better. Thanks.<br /><br />--<br /><br />Actual rating: <b>2.5 stars</b><br /><br />--<br /><br /><a href="http://aimeealways.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Aimee, Always</a> | <a href="http://twitter.com/aimeereads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/aimeereads" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4312679884067909863" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer572598755259700977"><b>Short Review:</b><br/><br/>I went into this with kinda mixed expectations––it sounds like Percy Jackson 2.0 (and well ... it kind of is), plus a bunch of my friends were disappointed by it. But honestly, it was better than I expected. It's no PJO, but I still really enjoyed it. Some thoughts:<br/><br/>- I actually don't know that much about Norse mythology, so it was a fun way to learn a bit about it––although I'm sure Rick Riordan took some liberties and glossed over some things. :P<br/>- I LOVE SAM, OH MY GOD. Why wasn't </span>
  <span id="freeText572598755259700977" style="display:none"><b>Short Review:</b><br><br>I went into this with kinda mixed expectations––it sounds like Percy Jackson 2.0 (and well ... it kind of is), plus a bunch of my friends were disappointed by it. But honestly, it was better than I expected. It's no PJO, but I still really enjoyed it. Some thoughts:<br><br>- I actually don't know that much about Norse mythology, so it was a fun way to learn a bit about it––although I'm sure Rick Riordan took some liberties and glossed over some things. :P<br>- I LOVE SAM, OH MY GOD. Why wasn't she the main character??? ... Like, seriously. I'm not kidding. <br>- Magnus is okay, but he's basically Percy all over again––except like, stupider and more annoying?? I feel like Percy was always endearingly clueless, but kinda got smarter as the books went on. But also he started off being 12 and Magnus is like 16, so I feel like he should've been a bit more mature. But I don't know––I don't hate him or anything, I just don't love him. Maybe he'll get cooler as the series continues. <br>- I love the setting in Boston because, having lived in the area pretty much my whole life, I actually knew all the places the book referenced. Woot woot! <br>- Also I loved the appearances of Annabeth, even if they were brief. I hope she shows up more in the series (and if other characters from PJO/HOO also ever show up, I will be very excited).<br>- THAT ENDING, MAN. It was intense. I'm excited to see what happens next. <br><br><b>Full Review:</b><br><br>Coming eventually.<br><br><b>Pre-review ranting/fangirling under the cut.</b><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><br>----------<br><br><b>6/3/15:</b><br><br>PSSST GUYS. Are you just going to write a series about every type of mythology in the world? Maybe you should try something new ... ?"<br><br>But, screw it. <b>I'M FUCKING PUMPED FOR THIS SERIES. AHHHHHHH.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418924820ra/12948983.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Reasons to be excited:<br><br>- Norse mythology!<br>- <b>IT TAKES PLACE IN BOSTONNNNN.</b> HELL YEAH, REPRESENTTT.<br>- Magnus <i>Chase</i>? As in Annabeth Chase????? Rick Riordan wouldn't just use the same last name without reason, <i><b>right</b></i>???? (Edit: Apparently he is Annabeth's cousin and this was referenced in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18705209.The_Blood_of_Olympus__The_Heroes_of_Olympus___5_" title="The Blood of Olympus (The Heroes of Olympus, #5) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Blood of Olympus</a> somewhere but I guess I missed it. Anyway ...   <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/903559999" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/903559999?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=guilty-pleasures">guilty-pleasures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=laugh-out-loud-humor">laugh-out-loud-humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=fearless-protagonists">fearless-protagonists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=copycat">copycat</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=typical">typical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=bubbling-under-5-stars">bubbling-under-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=razor-sharp-wheels">razor-sharp-wheels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=pants-are-snowmen-and-they-are-june">pants-are-snowmen-and-they-are-june</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer903559999" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5103650932655295449"><b>4.25 stars</b><br/><br/><blockquote>"Randolph shook his head in disgust. 'Those movies...ridiculously inaccurate. The real gods of Asgard—Thor, Loki, Odin, and the rest—are much more powerful, much more terrifying than anything Hollywood could concoct.'<br/><br/>'But...they're myths. They're not real.'<br/><br/>Randolph gave me a sort of pitying look. 'Myths are simply stories about truths we've forgotten.'"</blockquote><br/><br/>Yes, it's time for <b>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/732372672' rel='nofollow noopener'>another drinking game!</a>
</b> <br/><br/>The rules are simple. Each time something similar to Percy Jackson shows up and/or happen</span>
  <span id="freeText5103650932655295449" style="display:none"><b>4.25 stars</b><br><br><blockquote>"Randolph shook his head in disgust. 'Those movies...ridiculously inaccurate. The real gods of Asgard—Thor, Loki, Odin, and the rest—are much more powerful, much more terrifying than anything Hollywood could concoct.'<br><br>'But...they're myths. They're not real.'<br><br>Randolph gave me a sort of pitying look. 'Myths are simply stories about truths we've forgotten.'"</blockquote><br><br>Yes, it's time for <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/732372672" rel="nofollow noopener">another drinking game!</a>
</b> <br><br>The rules are simple. Each time something similar to Percy Jackson shows up and/or happens, take a shot. Try not to die of alcohol poisoning now, cause here we go!<br><br><b>Similarity #1 </b><br><br>The protagonist is a male sass master that can't be tamed.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451027386ra/17500493.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Similarity #2</b><br><br>Who is motherless because of Norse god-related reasons. She is a lovely lady, and he never knew his father.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451027386ra/17500494.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Similarity #3 </b><br>His female companion is experienced in the world of Norse mythology and doesn't like our dashing male lead at first.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451027386ra/17500495.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Similarity #4 </b><br>He travels with two comic relief characters, who are native magical characters a la Grover.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451027386ra/17500496.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Similarity #5 </b><br><br>They go on a quest to find a lost, very powerful magical item.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451028511ra/17500718.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Similarity #6 </b><br><br>Midway, they are unexpectedly taken out of action, leaving them with a slim window of time. Lotus Casino, anyone?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451028511ra/17500719.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Similarity #7 </b><br><br>Events cause them to question the morality compass of gods.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451028511ra/17500720.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Similarity #8 </b><br><br>He's betrayed by someone who thought to be a friend.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451028511ra/17500721.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Similarity #9 </b><br><br>His friends all have a secret painful past.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451028511ra/17500722.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Similarity #10 </b><br><br>Norse mythology is fucking real and hidden under humanity's noses for centuries. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451028511ra/17500723.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Similarity #11 </b><br><br>Norse gods are silly, per Riordan tradition. Thor, in particular, is fond of Game of Thrones.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451028511ra/17500724.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Still standing? Don't look so happy yet—We still have a <b>bonus round.</b> Drink if you spot a Percy Jackson reference.<br><br><b>PJ reference #1</b><br><br>Annabeth is his cousin. She and her dad make not-so-brief cameos.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451028511ra/17500725.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>PJ reference #2</b><br><br>Pen-sword.<br><br><blockquote>"The sword pulsed, almost like it was laughing. I imagined it saying,<i> A pen sword. That is the stupidest thing I've ever heard."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451027386ra/17500497.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>PJ reference #3</b><br><br>Jason Grace's name appears in a chapter title.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451028511ra/17500726.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>PJ reference #4</b><br><br>The series name: Magnus Chase and the Gods of Asgard/Percy Jackson &amp; the Olympians. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451028511ra/17500727.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Alright, let's get serious. I may bitch and moan about The Sword of Summer, but the truth is, I really liked it. Sam (Magnus's female questing companion) is a badass Muslim with a hajib and although I'm sure Riordan penned this before the Paris attacks, I'm glad she exists as a positive role model in a climate of Islamphobia. <br><br>Arranged marriages aren't portrayed as a contract with the devil. These days, most require enthusiastic consent from the bride and groom themselves. It's more like a blind date, except it's your parents talking up his job and house.<br><br>Annabeth's appearances are kept to a minimum, which is a relief. I laughed out loud on more than one occasion and enjoyed learning about Norse mythology. Reading Riordan's stuff is like slipping on a pair of comfy old sneakers.<br><br>Am I proud of it? No. Riordan is capable of so much more than a formula of random mythology, juvenile humor, and contemporary references. (Btw, <i>love</i> the nod to Taylor Swift. What? I'm a huge fan) I want him to do something totally different. I want to stop writing Percy Jackson books, dammit, and set a new story in a new universe.<br><br>But I guess I'm destined to be a hypocrite because I can't wait to get my hands on <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27904311.The_Hammer_of_Thor__Magnus_Chase_and_the_Gods_of_Asgard___2_" title="The Hammer of Thor (Magnus Chase and the Gods of Asgard, #2) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hammer of Thor</a>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451027386ra/17500498.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1478432310" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of The Hammer of Thor</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1478432316" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of The Ship of the Dead</a><br><br><b>Blurb reveal</b>: Is it just me or does this sound a hell lot like Percy Jackson? Troubled kid, son of a god, ancient enemies are stirring, must find a magical object or the world will end... Still gonna read it (duh), but it makes a girl wonder.<br><br><b>Pre-review:</b> Hmm... I was hoping for a girl narrator, but I have a feeling we'll be seeing Annabeth <s>and Percy. Oh, God, give me the boy.</s> later on, so that's forgiven. Hopefully, Magnus can redeem his name from another fictional character from a series I'm not very fond of.<br><br>And some of this would be lovely:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1402543130ra/9952149.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="5103650932655295449" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1082242386" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1082242386" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1082242386?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780141342412" href="/book/show/25090719-the-sword-of-summer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=magical-fantasy">magical-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=ya-without-romance">ya-without-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=ya-male-narrators">ya-male-narrators</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1082242386" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5361858580589115278"><b>That was HILARIOUS.</b> Like incredibly, marvellously FUNNY. I mean, it's Rick Riordan, right?! So you expect that...but I think this is one of his most goldenest books for humour ever (although granted I haven't read The Kane Chronicles yet, so we'll see how they match up!). <b>Basically I'm endlessly pleased with this hilarious novel of Magnus Chase.</b> It felt different from Percy Jackson, but still had the same vibe and hilarity (!!) and also ANNABETH HAS A CAMEO. Magnus Chase is Annabeth's cousin. Sh</span>
  <span id="freeText5361858580589115278" style="display:none"><b>That was HILARIOUS.</b> Like incredibly, marvellously FUNNY. I mean, it's Rick Riordan, right?! So you expect that...but I think this is one of his most goldenest books for humour ever (although granted I haven't read The Kane Chronicles yet, so we'll see how they match up!). <b>Basically I'm endlessly pleased with this hilarious novel of Magnus Chase.</b> It felt different from Percy Jackson, but still had the same vibe and hilarity (!!) and also ANNABETH HAS A CAMEO. Magnus Chase is Annabeth's cousin. She hasn't got a big part, nope, but she's <i>there</i> and it's makes me pleased. <br /><br />Ohhh, but WHERE TO START!! All I want to do is fangirl basically. But let me be logical here. I CAN DO THIS. How about a list?! THAT SHOULD HELP.<br /><br /><b>THE REASONS WHY THIS BOOK IS JUST DOWNRIGHT FABULOUS:</b><br /><br />+ Magnus Chase. He's a dork. He's really dramatic and funny and so so sarcastic. He has a sarcastic comeback for <i>everything</i> and it's just so fun to read. He's also really laid back. So yeah, he's dead -- okay dude, let's deal. Oh and now he has some cool powers -- got this. And let's just add in a going to a crazy Norse afterlife -- chillin'. <br /><br />+ THE CHAPTER TITLES. I <i>loved</i> them. They're ridiculously funny. Like "I Do Combat with Eggs" and "We Are Falafel-Jacked By An Eagle" and "We Have a Pre-Decapitation Party, with Egg Rolls" and "Don't Be a No-bro, Bro". Excuse me, I must giggle.<br /><br />+ The gods are equally quirky and insane and kooky as in the PJO books. Thor is a TV addict. He bypasses crushing an enemy to catch up with Game of Thrones, basically. And Odin sucks at giving speeches. One of the villainous monsters is a weird bag-lady. <br /><br />+ And there's actually no romance. NONE, PEOPLES. NOT A SCRAP. Which is just...weird. I was really, really surprised... Of course Magnus' buddy is Samirah al-Abbas, but she's in love with someone else! SO YEAH. How's that?!?<br /><br />+ But we gotta speak about the CHARACTERS! Of course! So Magnus' dorky sass is complimented by Samirah al-Abbas' seriousness and dedication to her job. She's a Valkyrie, so she guides heroes into the afterlife (I think is the jist of things) except it's so dubious whether Magnus is actually a hero or not that...she kinda gets in trouble. bUT ENOUGH OF THAT. Sam is epic! She's a daughter of Loki, so she's got heaps of abilities, but she swears never to be beguiling like her dad. She's also prone to punching Magnus. Also she's Muslim and wears a hijab sometimes, which is also magical. <br /><br />+ And Magnus has these two buddies, homeless dudes, who are just HILARIOUS. Like they're not <i>really</i> homeless dudes, of course, but a dwarf/elf in disguise who protect Magnus. Um, kind of protect? They slapped a monster in the face a sign about ducks?? So kinda helpful? ANYWAY. One of them loves designing clothes and the other is deaf. SO THAT'S COOL. (Except, I have to admit, the deaf guy isn't at all realistic, because he gets everything everyone is saying. He signs, but no one else does. Dude, I'm sorry, but reading lips is woefully inaccurate and hard. SURE he's a magical being, but it's not realistic.)<br /><br /><b>So, it kind of has similarities with Percy Jackson? But I didn't even mind!</b> Just there's a battle girl (daughter of Odin) who is <i>so</i> like Clarisse, and then Sam was a little like Annabeth (though I thought Magnus was pretty different from Percy!) OH OH and of course the plot is:<i> here is a quest, go meet monsters, go fulfil it. </i> But I laughed so much and enjoyed it a lot I didn't even mind!<br /><br /><b>My only quibble is: it's too long.</b> I really HONESTLY think there are too many plot detours that, while they might be entertaining, they're not actually adding to the plot. I did get a bit bored in the last 1/3. I like concise books, is all.<br /><br /><b>ANOTHER SOLIDLY FANTASTIC RIORDAN BOOK!</b> This brings my Riordan eating-ness up to 11 books! I'm quite addicted. And while this is YA (Magnus is 16) I totally think it still suits a younger audience too. It's funny and exciting and really creative and I learnt SO MUCH about Norse mythology! (Apparently Loki isn't brothers with Thor?! And I didn't even KNOW a god called Frey existed, so yeah. Fabulous.) I CAN'T WAIT FOR MORE. And it doesn't have a horrific cliffhanger, so I feel quite calm to wait for the next book. HUZZAH, THANK YOU FOR SPARING MY DELICATE FEELS, RICK RIORDAN. <br /><br />*** QUOTES OF AWESOMENESS***<br /><i>...beware, these are from an ARC copy so may not be finalised versions...</i><br /><br /><blockquote>"Give me one answer," I said. "One <i>clear</i> answer, without the rambling and the history lectures. You said you knew my dad. Who is he?"<br />Randolph placed his hand over mine... "On my life, Magnus, I swear this is the truth: your father is a Norse god. Now, hurry. We're in a twenty-minute parking spot."</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"Then why don't you just say A.D.?"<br />"Because Anno Domini, <i>in the Year of our Lord</i>, is fine for Christians, but Thor gets a little upset. He still holds a grudge that Jesus never showed for the duel he challenged him to."<br />"Say what now?"</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"could you do a glamour and turn into something smaller?" I asked it. "Preferably not a chain, since it's no longer the 1990s?" <br />The sword didn't reply (duh), but I imagined it was humming at a more interrogative pitch, like, <i>Such as what?</i><br />"I dunno. Something pocket-sized and innocuous. A pen, maybe?"<br />The sword pulsed, almost like it was laughing. I imagined it saying, <i>A pen sword. That is the stupidest thing I've ever heard.</i></blockquote><br /><br />HA I SEE WHAT YOU DID THERE RICK RIORDAN.<br /><br /><blockquote>"Back up," I said. "What did Sam mean by <i>again</i>? You've lost your hammer before?"<br />"Once," Thor said. "Okay, twice. Three times if you count this time, which you shouldn't, because I am not admitting that the hammer is missing."</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"I, at least, will make sure you get a proper trial before the thanes cast your soul into Ginnungagap!"<br />Samirah and I exchanged glances. We didn't have time to be captured and sent back to Asgard. I definitely didn't have time to get my soul cast into a place I couldn't even pronounce.</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="5361858580589115278" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1238882999" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1238882999" />
    <a title="Evelyn (devours and digests words)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words"><img alt="Evelyn (devours and digests words)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556809829p2/38658747.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1238882999?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evelyn (devours and digests words)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evelyn (devours and digests words)" href="/user/show/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words">Evelyn (devours and digests words)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24172101-the-sword-of-summer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=cover-beauts">cover-beauts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=bagful-of-laughs">bagful-of-laughs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=underwhelming">underwhelming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=fantastical">fantastical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=mythology-and-folklores">mythology-and-folklores</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=writing-i-would-love-to-imitate">writing-i-would-love-to-imitate</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=overrated-tbh">overrated-tbh</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1238882999" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16712076902043207855"><b>Either my sense of fun and humour has wilted into nothingness or Rick Riordan has started to bore me with his repeating usage of storylines and familiar jokes.</b><br/><br/>I opt for the latter.<br/><br/>I like to think that I have a good sense of humour - <i>I like to laugh at every single tiny jokes</i> and it takes a lot to snuff out that side of me. Okay fine, to its credit <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15724396.The_Sword_of_Summer__Magnus_Chase_and_the_Gods_of_Asgard___1_' title='The Sword of Summer (Magnus Chase and the Gods of Asgard, #1) by Rick Riordan' rel='nofollow noopener'> Magnus Chase and The Sword of Summer</a> is funny (it certainly does has its stupid, ri-donkey-lous moments), but the humour instilled here did not succe</span>
  <span id="freeText16712076902043207855" style="display:none"><b>Either my sense of fun and humour has wilted into nothingness or Rick Riordan has started to bore me with his repeating usage of storylines and familiar jokes.</b><br><br>I opt for the latter.<br><br>I like to think that I have a good sense of humour - <i>I like to laugh at every single tiny jokes</i> and it takes a lot to snuff out that side of me. Okay fine, to its credit <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15724396.The_Sword_of_Summer__Magnus_Chase_and_the_Gods_of_Asgard___1_" title="The Sword of Summer (Magnus Chase and the Gods of Asgard, #1) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener"> Magnus Chase and The Sword of Summer</a> is funny (it certainly does has its stupid, ri-donkey-lous moments), but the humour instilled here did not succeed in impressing me - much less made me laugh. Usually when I go into a book written by Rick Riordan, I'd be anticipating for the belly laughter and the blissful fun that comes with it.<br><br>But instead I end up rolling my eyes to high heavens like <i>where have I heard this joke before?</i><br><br>I suppose when you have read more than 10+ books with the same story arcs by THE SAME AUTHOR -  one way or another you're going to outgrow them.<br><br>I turn out to be one of those people and it sucked BIG TIME because I ended up:<br><br>a) being <b>poker-faced</b> in the entire story. I had no reactions to the jokes (which consists of snarks, witty comebacks and lots of modern pop culture) or the big answer reveals - none. Everything just feel too goddamn repeated. Formulaic and methodical even.<br><br>b) feeling <b>underwhelmed</b> by the overused plotlines/story arcs.<br><br>In this book, a prophecy forewarned Ragnarok (end of days) and that a hero will walk into the picture and prevent/postpone that from happpening. So its a cycle, heroes must fight back wrathful gods/monsters who try to destroy them and take over the whole wide world. <br><br>Yada, yada, yada. You know the drill. <b>Nothing is fucking new here.</b><br><br>Moving on.<br><br>c) feeling <b>annoyed AND bored</b>... by the overused 'The Chosen Special Snowflake' trope and 1000x other tropes.<br><br>Gods, Riordan, if only you'd stop with the repetitions! It's getting <i>real old.</i><br><br>d) feeling <b>detached</b> from MANY characters here. Something that's never happened to me when it comes to Riordan's books. So the fact that I'm 'not feeling it' really, really blows.<br><br>Don't get me wrong, each one of the characters here are actually all wonderfully fleshed out well with their own quirks and personalities (I have a HUGE adoration for both elf and dwarf: Hearthstone &amp; Blitz) but they don't feel so fully developed.<br><br>I hate to compare this to Percy Jackson/Kane Chronicles/The Heroes of Olympus but <b>everything here reads to me like they're all remolded from the previous series only half-heartedly.</b><br><br><br>e) Getting real <b>pissy</b> at the 'question evading' move.<br><br>QUESTIONS ARE EVADED A LOT HERE. Which is something I notice Riordan has a habit of doing in all his written works.<br><br>Look, <b>if you want to ground my attention to a story, make sure you don't try to keep frustrating me with the obvious lack of answers</b>. That's what this book does a lot. Whenever Magnus Chase questions something/someone, other people would be on the verge of answering him then suddenly, something else happens and the book will be all...<i> "Sorry. Your question will have to wait! You'll get your answers soon - just keep reading!"</i><br><br>Talk about getting exasperated, man.<br><br><br>f) feeling <b>baffled and unimpressed</b> with the depictions of the Norse gods and goddesses. All myths and legends are laced with grimness and bloodshed but it was never that way here. Everything that's dark and grimy are watered down into a sillier, lighter version. <b>A part of me liked that Thor is a farting, TV show addict but another part of me longed for that kickass, majestic hammer wielding Norse god he was portrayed to be.</b><br><br>I truly was expecting something more <i>serious </i> here. I wanted the portrayal of the gods &amp; godesses to be legit. Can't everything and everyone not be made into a laughingstock for once? This is Young Adult, the audiences can handle a bit of seriousness. Let there be more bloodshed!<br><br><p>* * *</p><br>I can never ever come close to hate anything Riordan writes but I can be underwhelmed and let down. Maybe even bored. Bummer.<br><br>However, despite its many not-so-redeeming qualities, there are still a ton of stuffs that I can praise.<br> <br><br>• <b>This book deals with DIVERSITY &amp; EQUALITY (in the most unique way possible).</b> Here, we have a muslim female sidekick, Samirah Al-Abbas, who wears a magical(!) hijab and wields some serious axe-slashing skill. Oh, and she's also in an arranged marriage with her twice-removed cousin.<br><br>Surprise, surprise! Seriously, that don't happen often in many YA books.<br><br>Eventhough Riordan glossed over the subject, I find it a pleasant thing that he brought it up for his readers. God knows how most of us are almost completely ignorant on that subject.<br><br>When someone mentions human equality in races - that's seriously great. But here, <b>it's like the author himself has decided to humanize elves, giants and dwarves and that as much as us normal human beings, they deserve not to be excluded out or be stereotyped too.</b> (You'll get what I mean when you read the book)<br><br>• <b> The adventures never seem to s-t-o-p. They won't even let you have the liberty to pause and catch your breath</b> because in every chapters, there will always, always be some quest going on despite the fact that Ragnarok is looming around the corner.<br><br>What makes it most interesting is that these quests are often enlightening. <b>You'll learn a LOT of Norse myths along the way.</b><br><br>• <b>The awesome and ACCURATE imitation of a teenager's lifestyle and voice.</b> We all know Mr Riordan isn't a teenager but I swear, I think he may still be one because he realistically captured how a teenager would sound, behave and act like. The narration that comes from Magnus, a 16 year old, never felt so forced and it was easy for me to be able to just click with him.<br><br>Also, brace yourself for MANY mentions of modern pop cultures. (Featuring... Taylor Swift) Oh... and TV shows, too. <br><br>• <b>The HILARIOUS titles are back in the picture and they're most probably going to make you bend over chortling</b>.To the readers who have loyally followed Riordan's trails for years now will know what I'm talking about. This author is the MAN when it comes to chapter titles.<br><br><br>To wrap it up, this book was just fun and silly to read. I'd say educational, too. But other than that, a part of me has decided that it's probably time I outgrow Riordan's books (Hello, maturity!) and move on to a more serious myth-related stories. I will still read Magnus Chase's further adventures but something tells me that the magic and the fun I'd be feeling will not be so much anymore. <s>I'm totally not emotional right now.</s><br><br><i> See more reviews at... </i><br><a href="https://bookswithchemistry.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433653616i/15127136._SX540_.png" width="350" height="117" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="16712076902043207855" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
