<div id="review_2279458157" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2279458157" />
    <a title="Ashwood (애쉬 우드)." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50173624-ashwood"><img alt="Ashwood (애쉬 우드)." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596432515p2/50173624.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2279458157?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashwood (애쉬 우드)." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashwood (애쉬 우드)." href="/user/show/50173624-ashwood">Ashwood (애쉬 우드).</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2279458157" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15516613649494371994"> “Let’s take that hill!” He pointed to a nearby ridge at the edge of the woods. <br/> “Why?” I yelled. <br/> “Because it’s a hill!”<br/> “He loves taking hills,” Mallory grumble. “It’s a Civil War thing.”<br/><br/>I loved Magnus Chase! The dude was just priceless. His sarcasm and humor was outta this world hilarious. The way he reacted to half the situations he was put in, just had me cracking up several times throughout the story. <br/><br/>This was a super easy, exciting, witty and addicting read! The world building, plot twist</span>
  <span id="freeText15516613649494371994" style="display:none"> “Let’s take that hill!” He pointed to a nearby ridge at the edge of the woods. <br /> “Why?” I yelled. <br /> “Because it’s a hill!”<br /> “He loves taking hills,” Mallory grumble. “It’s a Civil War thing.”<br /><br />I loved Magnus Chase! The dude was just priceless. His sarcasm and humor was outta this world hilarious. The way he reacted to half the situations he was put in, just had me cracking up several times throughout the story. <br /><br />This was a super easy, exciting, witty and addicting read! The world building, plot twists, characters... just everything about it was awesome. I honestly, really really enjoyed this book. </span>

<div id="review_3304159787" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3304159787" />
    <a title="mwana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32149976-mwana"><img alt="mwana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599506706p2/32149976.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3304159787?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="mwana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="mwana" href="/user/show/32149976-mwana">mwana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24172101-the-sword-of-summer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32149976-mwana?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32149976-mwana?shelf=favorites-2020">favorites-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32149976-mwana?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3304159787" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4229465726522170708"><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>Myths are simply stories about truths we’ve forgotten.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/>HOLY SHIT this was AMAZING.<br/><br/>As I've mentioned before, I am emulating the noble ostrich in hiding between pages of beautiful prose and embarking on my career as a second hand adventurer. Magnus Chase is without a doubt one of the best YA heroes I've read about this year, ever, in fact.<br/><br/>I'm not inclined to talk about what this book is about because it's quite simply an urban fantasy adventure story based on Norse mythology. It has all</span>
  <span id="freeText4229465726522170708" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>Myths are simply stories about truths we’ve forgotten.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br />HOLY SHIT this was AMAZING.<br /><br />As I've mentioned before, I am emulating the noble ostrich in hiding between pages of beautiful prose and embarking on my career as a second hand adventurer. Magnus Chase is without a doubt one of the best YA heroes I've read about this year, ever, in fact.<br /><br />I'm not inclined to talk about what this book is about because it's quite simply an urban fantasy adventure story based on Norse mythology. It has all of my favorite tropes: the reluctant chosen one, the quest, found family, side quests, and an all powerful hero who could solve everything with a flick of his fingers but won't lift any because Game of Thrones (I really would like to see how he'd react to the season that shan't be named).<br /><br />Beyond being one of the best adventure stories I've had the fortune of reading in recent times, it was also really funny. Magnus, a falafel-loving Kurt Cobain lookalike, is an excellent and charming narrator.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>In front, a room-service cart sat in the hallway with the severed head of a pig on a silver platter. The pig’s ears and nose looked slightly nibbled. Now, I’m not a food critic. Being homeless, I could never afford to be. But I draw the line at pig heads.</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />The humour in this book doesn't sneak up on you. Right off the bat, Magnus is snarky, rude, sarcastic and has an inability to restrain himself from quipping that MCU Tony Stark would he proud of. <br /><br />Besides that, the found family is literally JUST THE BEST. I loved every one of them. I haven't loved ALL the characters in a piece of media since Avatar: The Last Airbender and you'd sooner ask me to pick a favorite potato before I had to choose among Blitzen who has an adorable (lifesaving, it's lifesaving) aversion to sunlight, Hearth who's basically a deaf young Gandalf who's fluent in Gesticulation and Samira, a Muslim Valkyrie and if that isn't the most badass thing ever, I don't know what is. Even the villains are amazing. They are charming, there is real peril, stakes and even lessons.<br /><br />I saw descriptions calling this an inclusive Percy Jackson and if that's the case, sign me up and call me a Magnus Chaser because honey, I need the rest of the series desperately. <br /><br />If for nothing else, then Thor's chariot goats. Perhaps Otis finally gets a chance to unload the breakthroughs he's gotten from his therapy sessions. Or to see what other manner of human corporate communication skills Odin manages to uncover next. <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“I am a seeker of knowledge!” Odin announced. <br /><br />“This has always been true. I hung from the World Tree for nine days and nights, racked with pain, in order to discover the secret of runes. I stood in line in a blizzard for six days to discover the sorcery of the smartphone.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />I really can't wait to read the sequels. This just became one of my favorite series of all time. At least 2020 is amounting to something.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4229465726522170708" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1091186282" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7077060549178924928">Rick can't do wrong. Another adventure of epic proportions lead by the incredibly sarcastic Magnus is not "just another" Percy Jackson, but a distinctive and a little bit more grown-up journey featuring dwarves, elves, Valkyries and of course, the master of mischief Loki and his many godly opponents. Hilariously written with a fast-paced plot and diverse and powerful characters. Addictive!<br/><br/>Advanced reading copy provided by Penguin </span>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1510785994?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1510785994" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18222610757542693438">Reading Percy Jackson now, making me feel I was right here. Percy Jackson better Urban Fantasy, this one a bit higher or wilder.<br/><b>A Breakneck, Jam-Packed Roller Coaster of an Adventure..<br/></b><i>’I Know It's Jo’s Blurb for House of Secrets, but sorry, Can't help but use it here too’</i><b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454285571i/17940569._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='504' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>The All-The-Ancient-Gods Geek, Rick Riordan takes us in a new Adventure Up and Down the Tree of Laeradr,Worlds of Asgard’s Gods & Viking Myths.<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454285721i/17940612._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='559' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>With a Variety of resourceful characters..<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454289142ra/17940908.gif' width='400' height='283' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Oh and don't forget the Hotel Valhalla, </b>suc</span>
  <span id="freeText18222610757542693438" style="display:none">Reading Percy Jackson now, making me feel I was right here. Percy Jackson better Urban Fantasy, this one a bit higher or wilder.<br><b>A Breakneck, Jam-Packed Roller Coaster of an Adventure..<br></b><i>’I Know It's Jo’s Blurb for House of Secrets, but sorry, Can't help but use it here too’</i><b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454285571i/17940569._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="504" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The All-The-Ancient-Gods Geek, Rick Riordan takes us in a new Adventure Up and Down the Tree of Laeradr,Worlds of Asgard’s Gods &amp; Viking Myths.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454285721i/17940612._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="559" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>With a Variety of resourceful characters..<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454289142ra/17940908.gif" width="400" height="283" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Oh and don't forget the Hotel Valhalla, </b>such a lovely place (such a lovely place), such a lov...sorry.<b><br>It's a fun story really, almost perfectly summed up by the ending as;</b><i>
  <blockquote>
<br>‘I considered everything I’d been through – death and resurrection, fishing for the World Serpent, fighting with giants, running from monster squirrels, binding a wolf on a disappearing island’</blockquote>
</i>BUT -with a quick look at all the other reviews, Goodreads clearly must add the Half Star to the ratings.- My rating is just <b>3.5, </b>-to give it 4 is too much for my overall liking-<br>It's 2.5 Story , 3.5 Characters , 4.5 insightful look into the Norse Myths and Gods. -which was better than the Marvel Movies insight in a way.-<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454286500ra/17940668.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>But again that isn't fair putting it that way, the story has some good points, and many weak ones..<br>So does the characters, some are strongly written and some just normal.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454289815i/17940960._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="573" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>And here ,and so later, I must say drawing a Muslim Girl in this kind of fantasy is extraordinary perfectly written ,one of the points that made me love the series more..</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454286661i/17940685.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><a href="http://annabethisterrified.tumblr.com/post/131326935181/st00pzdraws-samirah-al-abbas-valkyrie" rel="nofollow noopener">This amazing drowning can be found in this lovely blog</a><br><b><br>So let's see why it was a real ‘Roller Coaster’ as I said in the beginning of this review, let's see What was Up and what was Down…<br><br><blockquote>DOWN</blockquote>
<br>**Meet Magnus ,&amp; his street friends ,but Mind all the sarcasm.</b><br>reminded me strongly of Percy Jackson in the first few pages I have read for him..,I may used to his sarcasm later, may found some of it funny later..but that wasn't that good starting.<br>So from now on...I'll try to Review it as Magnus..<b><br><br><blockquote>UP</blockquote>
<br>**Oh, he's a Demigod</b> -Perrrrcyyyy-<b> Thanks to his Uncle's insightful speech of the Norse Gods.</b><br>The speech and the theory of the Viking discovered North America first is interesting, and the Boston history, I just love it. -specially I've read this theory in a Donald Duck comic adventure by Carl Barks back in the 50s.<b><i><br><blockquote>“Myths are simply stories about truths we've forgotten.”</blockquote></i><br><blockquote>DOWN</blockquote>
<br>**That's how to get a 2000 years lost Sword???<br><br>**A Catastrophic Fire Giant Fight in the middle of real world????<br><br>**Oh, and the Agony Death to complete the day !, just as promised.<br><br><blockquote>UP</blockquote>
<br>**Welcome to the Hotel Valhalla ,<i>Such a lovely place (Such a lovely place), Such a lovely faaaaceee.</i></b><br>Though it wasn't my cup of coffee to read a dead character story ,but hey it's ancient Gods story , so suck it..<b><br><br>**A Tour in the Norse Heaven…<br></b>I loved how Uncle Rick made it so vivid.<br><br><b>**The Valkariy Samirah al-Abbas and the disastrous dinner.<br></b>Sorting Hat anyone?<b><br><br><blockquote>Still UP</blockquote>
<br>**Plenty of room at the Hotel Valhalla, <i>Any time of year (Any time of year),You can find it here.</i></b><br>I just loved the Norse myth and how Rick Riordan take us there professionally , Yet I have this unsettling feeling..<br><b>"This could be Heaven or this could be Hell"</b><br>But still , I just like the variety of the company, also liked that you can always break the rules and leaving the Hotel… got too much potential but alas, it didn't put in use just 2,3 chapters later..<br><b>And she said "We are all just prisoners here, of our own device"<br><br>**Oh ,and here comes Loki.<br><br><blockquote>DOWN</blockquote>
<br>**Escaping Hotel California, sorry, Valhalla..<br><br>**The Truth of Magnus’ Friends, the Elf and the Dwarf.<br></b>I just used the characters of the hotel, you know, the crazy half naked Viking ,and the smart sarcastic a bit girl… well… at least Samirah will be there.<br><br><b>**Attending the funeral..of himself.<br><br><blockquote>UP</blockquote>
<br>**The Quest; <u>Magnus, you must find the Sword, God knows where now,and you must Stop the Norse Armagadone ,by restraining a Wolf God knows how, in an Island that only appear in , whatever he got only Nine Days, God knows where..<br>And remember...every one tell you any lead you must pay certain cost, Gods Knows How..<i>sometimes they themselves who ask for that</i></u><br><br><blockquote>DOWN</blockquote>
<br>**...said a severed head, sorry, a God !<br><br>**A Giant Eagle in a Food Court, Kidnapping Magnus.<br></b>Too much weird fantasy in real world...I love things more like, Ministry of Magic secure if you know what I mean..<b><br><br><blockquote>UP</blockquote>
<br>**I -Me ,really- love Samirah al-Abbas.</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454289142i/17940907._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="283" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The author really wrote it very well and very respectfully to the real moderated Muslim's lifestyle. Total respect. 2 of my best friends here -real YA, Big RR fans- told me the author researched deeply in the Muslim books to get understanding terms for Samirah , and I gotta say that though the flying Hijab was a bit too much, but otherwise I just can't appreciate the author enough..<br><i>PS: A novel later, Ink and Bone, has also a Muslim girl, smart and good and all...but just not as real as here.</i><b><br>**oh , and Hearthstone is quite fine too.<br><br><blockquote>Still UP</blockquote>
<br>**Go Fisihing the World Serpent.<br><br>**Meet a freaky geeky collector Goddess.<br></b>Magnus was really smart here.<b><br><br>**The Tree of Learadr<br><br><blockquote>DOWN</blockquote>
<br>**Hello, MILF, sorry, Aunt. <i>Who also my best friend’s Mom.</i><br><br>**The Dwarfs contests and Rules are the most ridiculous thing ,ever.<br></b>Blitz can be my least favorite character , his obsession about fashion so overused.<br><br><b>**And again, more enemies for live..<br><br>**A Talking Sword, A Talking Sword...<br><br><blockquote>UP</blockquote>
<br>**Loki again, in the most disgusting set.<br></b>I honestly love the information about the Norse ancient myths.<br><br><b>**And meet The Funniest Talking Goat ever..</b><br>Creepy, funny, depressed goat ever...just kill it, sorry ,like it. , reminded me a bit with Shrek's Donkey.<b><br>&amp;<br>**Have you met Thor?<br><br><blockquote>DOWN</blockquote>
<br>**Okay ,Thor is not the movies’ handsome macho hot guy...we get it, but you don't need to keep fart it.</b><br>Really horrible.<br><b>**KILLING GIANTS SISTERS AT THEIR HOME.<br></b>No matter what happened, no matter what their other sister did, no matter a damn thing that was stupid and brutal and not Good Middle Grade or even YA read.<br><b><br>**GUESS WHAT, TALKING SWORDS CAN'T SEE A JACK.<br><br><blockquote>Still DOWN</blockquote>
<br>** MORE Giants Killing.</b><br>No seriously, at least George R.R. Martian has a point writing the Red Wedding @ A Storm of Swords.. <br>I have to admit, through all the ups and downs ,the part of the giants is the thing that really really stopped me rate it more than 3.<br>I Understand killing a Giant trying to drown a God!!!! , but plotting an escape by killing a whole family in their home is just the ridiculous of all.<b><br><br><blockquote>UP</blockquote>
<br>**The Hummer of Thor is...spoiler. and A NETFLEX.<br></b>Thor is so fun , I strangely find I just like him in some things..<i>
  <br>
  <blockquote>‘Won’t you come with us? This is an important battle – the fire lord Surt, Fenris Wolf. Surely that’s worthy of your attention.’ <br> Thor’s right eye twitched. ‘That’s a fine offer. Really. I’d love to, but I have another pressing appointment –’ <br> ‘Game of Thrones,’ Marvin explained. <br> ‘Shut up!’ Thor raised his staff over our heads.</blockquote>
</i><br>Oh, Marvin is the Goat I told you about.<br><b><br><blockquote>UPs &amp; DOWNs , Right &amp; Left</blockquote>
<br>** The Climax, the Wolf, The back of the hall mates, The Dome theory , the prolong anti-climax… and Who's the Hell is Annabeth ,and why should he lose the bet? Did she a fan of Game of Thrones too and watched ‘em all?<br></b><br>Okay ,yes after I finish it I got it that Annabeth is a Percy Jackson character , so I lose a bet.<br>The ending is sure mostly Up more than Down… but wasn't high enough due to some of the very down hell.<br><b><br>Finally<br>-----<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454289815i/17940961._SY540_.png" width="400" height="557" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Even if I didn't appreciate some of the over-doused fantasy here </b>-Oh no, I may be really getting older :(-<b> I still loved the insightful look into the Myths of the Norse.. <br>And I have to thank my dearest friends here Malak and Raoofa for encouraging me to this world ,Worlds, of Rick Riordan...the all ancient Gods Master..<br> </b><br>And one final small thing… wasn't cool at all bringing Jesus to the Gods of Asgard… I mean just why? , why not one of the Greek Gods, Egyptian ones or whatever.<br><blockquote>“Because Anno Domini, in the Year of Our Lord, is fine for Christians, but Thor gets a little upset. He still holds a grudge that Jesus never showed up for that duel he challenged him to.” “Say what now?” </blockquote><br><b><br>Anyway, As I said at the beginning, it was A Breakneck, Jam-Packed Roller Coaster of an Adventure.. Comes Complete with a variety of characters, some are awesome written, some are good enough and some are, just Jack.<br>And I am really waiting for book Two...and wishing the Roller Coaster takes me Up and Down more, but just Keeps me feel Higher all the time.<br></b><br>Mohammed Arabey<br>From 15 January 2016<br>To 22 January 2016</span>

<div id="review_1406678299" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1406678299" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1406678299?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=laughing-to-the-bank">laughing-to-the-bank</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=sometimes-fun-beats-profound">sometimes-fun-beats-profound</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1406678299" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17790394045150068979">This is the first book in Riordan's Norse series (though you'll meet a few old friends from the Percy Jackson series along the way). The third and last book in this trilogy, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28006120.The_Ship_of_the_Dead__Magnus_Chase_and_the_Gods_of_Asgard___3_' title='The Ship of the Dead (Magnus Chase and the Gods of Asgard, #3) by Rick Riordan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Ship of the Dead</a>, has just been published. Full review, originally published on <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.fantasyliterature.com'>www.fantasyliterature.com:</a> <br/><br/>Rick Riordan, who has enthralled millions of readers with exciting tales of teenagers and their interactions with Greek, Roman and Egyptian gods and goddesses, turns to Norse mythology in his latest book, <i>The Sword </i></span>
  <span id="freeText17790394045150068979" style="display:none">This is the first book in Riordan's Norse series (though you'll meet a few old friends from the Percy Jackson series along the way). The third and last book in this trilogy, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28006120.The_Ship_of_the_Dead__Magnus_Chase_and_the_Gods_of_Asgard___3_" title="The Ship of the Dead (Magnus Chase and the Gods of Asgard, #3) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Ship of the Dead</a>, has just been published. Full review, originally published on <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com">www.fantasyliterature.com:</a> <br><br>Rick Riordan, who has enthralled millions of readers with exciting tales of teenagers and their interactions with Greek, Roman and Egyptian gods and goddesses, turns to Norse mythology in his latest book, <i>The Sword of Summer</i>. <br><br>Magnus Chase is sixteen years old and has been homeless for two years, since his mother died. Magnus remembers the door of their apartment splintering and wolves with glowing blue eyes bursting in as his mother shooed him out the fire escape. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444804078i/16555932.jpg" width="300" height="224" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>His mother had always told him to avoid his uncles, especially Uncle Randolph, so Magnus, naturally, runs into Randolph, who somehow convinces Magnus to accompany him to retrieve an ancient sword from the waters below Longfellow Bridge in Boston. Magnus magically calls the sword to himself. Unfortunately, it’s a corroded, slimy, barnacle-encrusted piece of metal with no hilt. Worse, a fireball-wielding man promptly appears and demands, whilst incinerating various items on the bridge, that Magnus give him the sword. <br><br>It’s not entirely surprising that Magnus dies in their confrontation ― particularly since Magnus announces on the first page that he dies. It’s a little more surprising when Magnus regains consciousness on the doorstep of the luxurious Hotel Valhalla, where the einherjar (heroes who have died in battle) live until Ragnarok, the final great battle at the end of the world. In Hotel Valhalla, the minibar is always stocked, the gigantic Tree of Laeadr grows in the dining hall, and einherjar gleefully die glorious, bloody deaths in daily battles, from which they are promptly resurrected. The display board in the hotel lobby informs Magnus of each day’s activities:<br><br>SINGLE COMBAT TO THE DEATH! – OSLO ROOM, 10 A.M.<br>GROUP COMBAT TO THE DEATH! – STOCKHOLM ROOM, 11 A.M.<br>BUFFET LUNCH TO THE DEATH! – DINING HALL, 12 P.M.<br>BIKRAM YOGA TO THE DEATH! – COPENHAGEN ROOM, BRING YOUR OWN MAT, 4 P.M.<br><br>Predictably, Magnus’ fate is not to simply <s>rest</s> fight in Valhalla. He is soon off on a quest, encouraged by some gods, hunted by others who are trying to capture or kill him, and assisted by a charmingly diverse group of friends, including his former Valkyrie Samirah, a hijab-wearing Muslim human girl with some extraordinary powers; Blitzen, a dwarf whose creativity runs to fashion design; and Hearthstone, a deaf elf with a hard-won magical talent and family issues. <br><br>Riordan skillfully weaves together a rousing adventure, constant humor, and interesting bits of Norse mythology, some more familiar than others. Characters such as Surt, Frey and Fenris Wolf, and legendary items such as Gleipnir (the chain that binds Fenris) and Naglfar, the Ship of Nails, were new to me, but have their roots in Norse mythology. Familiar Asgard gods such as Thor, Loki and Odin also show up in the pages of <i>The Sword of Summer</i>, though these characters’ appearance and personalities may raise the eyebrows of readers who are primarily familiar with their Marvel counterparts. There are a few sly references to Riordan’s prior series, such as cameo appearances by Annabeth (who will be familiar to Percy Jackson fans), that tie this new series into the same universe as <i>Percy Jackson and the Olympians</i>.<br><br>Although <i>The Sword of Summer</i> is overall a light-hearted adventure tale, it incorporates the violence that was part of the Viking culture. It also deals with the issue of homelessness in a way that’s not too heavy, but doesn’t sidestep the problems and troubles of those who are homeless, such as their inability to keep themselves and their clothing clean, their invisibility to members of society, and the suspiciousness that often becomes part of a homeless person’s personality.<br><br>You're not going to get anything startlingly new or deeply profound with <i>The Sword of Summer</i>; it's in the same vein as his prior young adult books, the literary equivalent of Variations on a Theme. Magnus' personality is pretty much interchangeable with Percy's. But it's an entertaining novel with plenty of action and laugh out loud humor. Quirky chapter titles like "Make Way for Ducklings, or They Will Smack You Upside the Head" and "Come to the Dark Side. We Have Pop-Tarts" made me chuckle, as did Odin’s transformation (thanks to a week-long seminar) into a cheesy motivational speaker. On a more personal note, my own children’s enthusiasm for both reading and mythology took a big turn upwards with Rick Riordan’s books, and I’ll always be grateful for that. My 13 year old son Tyler couldn’t even wait for me to finish writing this review to swipe the book away from me.<br><br>This would be a 3 or 3.5 star book for me personally, as a more critical adult, but I'm going with 4 stars based on the intended audience. Fans of the <i>Percy Jackson</i> series will be more than satisfied with <i>The Sword of Summer</i>, which is the first book in a projected trilogy called <i>Magnus Chase and the Gods of Asgard</i>. Tyler and I will both be anxiously awaiting the next installment in this series.<br><br><b>Initial post:</b><br>YES! Yes, yes, yes!! The ARC of the hardback just got delivered to my house!<br><br>My 13 year old son will think I'm the coolest mom <b>EVER</b>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17790394045150068979" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1318210119" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1318210119" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1318210119?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141342429" href="/book/show/25909686-the-sword-of-summer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=fantastic-lit-and-co">fantastic-lit-and-co</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1318210119" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11837907779503424664"><i>“To Cassandra Clare<br/>Thanks for letting me share the excellent name Magnus.”</i><br/><br/>No joking. I swear on all the books I own that this is the actual dedication of this book. <br/><br/><br/><b>“The <i>once warriors</i>-the warriors who fought bravely in the last life and will fight bravely again on the Day of Doom. Duck.”<br/>“The Day of Doom Duck?”<br/>“No, duck!”<br/>Hunding pushed me down as a spear flew past.”</b><br/><br/>Seriously, how am I supposed to review a book that contains quotes like this?<br/><br/>In truth, there are very few thing you need to know abou</span>
  <span id="freeText11837907779503424664" style="display:none"><i>“To Cassandra Clare<br>Thanks for letting me share the excellent name Magnus.”</i><br><br>No joking. I swear on all the books I own that this is the actual dedication of this book. <br><br><br><b>“The <i>once warriors</i>-the warriors who fought bravely in the last life and will fight bravely again on the Day of Doom. Duck.”<br>“The Day of Doom Duck?”<br>“No, duck!”<br>Hunding pushed me down as a spear flew past.”</b><br><br>Seriously, how am I supposed to review a book that contains quotes like this?<br><br>In truth, there are very few thing you need to know about <i>The Sword of Summer</i>. I'll try to recap them for you as briefly and clearly as possible:<br><br><b>1) </b>Does Riordan use and reuse all the schemes he already used in <i><b>Percy Jackson and the Olympians</b>,</i> <i>
  <b>The Heroes of Olympus</b>
</i> and the<i>
  <b>Kane Chronicles</b>
</i>?<br>Yes, and you all already knew that, so no need for me to linger on the topic.<br><br><b>2)</b> Does Magnus Chase resemble, in attitude and personality, Percy Jackson? <br>But of course my dears.<br><br><b>3)</b> Did I hopelessly fall (again) for Magnus's sense of humor just as I fell for Percy's? <br>Hell (lol) yes!<br><br><b>4)</b> Do I give a darn about Mr Riordan's repetitiveness as long as he manages to make me double up with laughter?<br>Absolutely not!<br><br>If you are looking for something <i>different</i>, people, don't pick up this book. But if you're looking for an<b> intelligent</b>,<b> well-written</b>, impossibly<b> funny </b>and <b>hilarious</b> middle-grade book, with <b>characters</b> so realistic, relatively complex, and easy to connect with, with a plot that is so fast-paced as to not give you time to catch you breath, then this (or any other Riordan book, for that matter) truly is the best you'll ever do.<br><br>The only thing that somewhat bothered me concerns the characters: there are really many of them, and maybe that's the reason why I struggled to make myself care for those of them who don't get much screen time, namely the <b>Valhalla Hotel gang</b> (TJ, Mallory, Halfborn and) X. It's particularly sad because these are, coincidentally, also the ones I was most curious about. I hope they get bigger roles in the next books.<br><br>On the other hand, I completely loved each and every one of Magnus's quest companions. They more or less all represent fresh additions in Riordan's inventory, and each of them can boast a pretty solid background story. More specifically, <b>Sam</b> is probably nothing exceptional in terms of characterisation, but <b>Hearth</b> and <b>Blitz</b>, the elf and the dwarf, are marvellous. It breaks me that they probably won't be present in the next installments, or at least not as much as they were in this one. <br><br>And the villains! I seriously hope that <i>The Hammer of Thor</i> will regale us with more <b>Loki</b>. We want <b>Loki</b>. <b>Loki</b> is our king. And yes, he's so cool, his name should always be written in bold. Just because. Like, <b>Loki</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445633072ra/16683144.gif" width="420" height='230"' alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451883035ra/17616265.gif" width="420" height='230"' alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And to go out with a bang, another little hidden jewel. It's not properly a quote, but a chapter title. If you've never read Riordan, really, people, you can't even imagine what this man can do with chapter titles. He completely redefines the whole category. Exhibit A, the masterpiece that introduces chapter 48:<br><br><b>"Hearthstone Passes Out Even More than Jason Grace (Though I Have No Idea Who That Is)"</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="11837907779503424664" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1078742253" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1078742253" />

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1078742253?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophia" href="/user/show/3766576-sophia">Sophia</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1078742253" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1117579121719695911">jam! it did take a bit for me to actually get into the story and i don't think anyone can say that riordan's novels aren't at least a little formulaic, but the cast of characters is refreshing and the plot is non-stop (*sings hamilton in my head*). i think the book gets better the more you read and by the end, i was sad to see it was over. also, i cried at the last handful of chapters. i'm a huge mess sorry. </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1519449524" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1519449524" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1519449524?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=1-star-reads">1-star-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=y-a">y-a</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1519449524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8180059485647069215">I gave up at the point where the homeless kids shot some giant fire destruction daemon type thing with a plastic cupid bow and arrow. <br/><br/><b>I mean, seriously? That actually happened? </b><br/><br/>That ruined it for me. I’m all up for humour in books, but when the humour seeps into what I consider a serious situation of life and death, it becomes a little bit too stupid. It just didn’t feel real. Bare with me a moment here. There is a giant fire daemon that has emerged in an otherwise normal world, there’s nothing </span>
  <span id="freeText8180059485647069215" style="display:none">I gave up at the point where the homeless kids shot some giant fire destruction daemon type thing with a plastic cupid bow and arrow. <br /><br /><b>I mean, seriously? That actually happened? </b><br /><br />That ruined it for me. I’m all up for humour in books, but when the humour seeps into what I consider a serious situation of life and death, it becomes a little bit too stupid. It just didn’t feel real. Bare with me a moment here. There is a giant fire daemon that has emerged in an otherwise normal world, there’s nothing wrong with that, but the danger didn’t feel real. Okay, so the protagonist may die in the encounter, though it wasn’t a real death. <br /><br />It was more of a case of ‘Oh, I’m dead. This is cool. Let’s see what happens next. It might me fun. I’m a stupid teenager btw. I’m like, totally, self-absorbed. I’m that awesome that I don’t even care that I’m dead. Screw you world. ’ <br /><br />There wasn’t really any sense of seriousness about it. If I was fighting some evil hell type spawn, I would like to think I wouldn’t act with a high degree of nonchalance. It’s like the protagonist shrugs his shoulders and doesn’t give a fuck about his imminent death. It made the situation a little bizarre. Magnus is your typical sarcastic teenager. He’s the type that has nothing but shitty comments up his sleeve and stupid innuendos. We all know the kind of guy I mean, and on a personal level, I find this type of personality rather <b>annoying. </b>I certainly don’t want to read an entire book where this douche bag is the narrator. No thank you. So I gave up. I wasn’t going to waste my time finishing a book I knew I’d dislike. <br /><br />The writing isn’t bad. It is heavily character driven. But, when you don’t like the said character then you know this isn’t going to work for you. It’s only going to get worse as time goes on. I also found the idea of Magnus being the decedent of some ancient Norse God a little bit crappy. It’s the type of idea I’d expect to see in some lame-ass b movie on the science fiction channel. The blending of ancient history with a modern world has always seemed a little bit forced to me, and, well, <b>a little bit cheesy</b>. There are few things I’d like to read less than a story about a moronic teenager being gifted with random ancient powers that he doesn’t understand or deserve. I like my history in the past. And I like my characters with redeeming personalities, not flat in their singular defensive attitude. Gosh…..I hate teenagers like this. <br /><br />This author is <b>
  <u>sooooooooooooooooo not for me</u>
</b>. Judging by the blurbs of his other books, and comparisons by other reviewers with his previous books, all his stories are pretty much based on this single idea. I won’t be reading anything else by Rick Riorden in the future because I know I will dislike it. Never again will I try his books, I’ve got better things to read. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8180059485647069215" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('N0sCjeLMKQECSOl3wvkvvXQCRHDQQ4ZA0eAGpVu3gscNbWtfWZLgaaVjXRY1DCViol2juB7OCCeKnkAUlvRwXQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('AlwuKL04D5LChCGBtTaZayGSFlJ7YXYqeTsB8Hgm4QE4ekf6BmbG+mWvleBCw5O0983xmrXs+E0iRUdBtWUTmw==')})
  }

But he has strong and steadfast friends, including Hearthstone the elf, Blitzen the dwarf, and Samirah the Valkyrie, and together they have achieved brave deeds, such as defeating Fenris Wolf and battling giants for Thor\'s hammer, Mjolnir. Now Magnus faces his most dangerous trial yet. His cousin, Annabeth, recruits her boyfriend, Percy Jackson, to give Magnus some pointers, but will his training be enough?\n\nLoki is free from his chains. He\'s readying Naglfar, the Ship of the Dead, complete with a host of giants and zombies, to sail against the Asgardian gods and begin the final battle of Ragnarok. It\'s up to Magnus and his friends to stop him, but to do so they will have to sail across the oceans of Midgard, Jotunheim, and Niflheim in a desperate race to reach Naglfar before it\'s ready to sail. Along the way, they will face angry sea gods, hostile giants, and an evil fire-breathing dragon. But Magnus\'s biggest challenge will be facing his own inner demons. Does he have what it takes to outwit the wily trickster god?<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"420997432268415023\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n       <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/21400019-the-sword-of-summer">Quotes from The Sword of Summer</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Myths are simply stories about truths we've forgotten.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/7296058-myths-are-simply-stories-about-truths-we-ve-forgotten">290 likes</a>

            <div class="clear"></div>

          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Could you do a glamour and turn into something smaller?" I asked it. "Preferably not a chain, since it's no longer the 1990s?"<br /><br />The sword didn't reply (duh), but I imagined it was humming at a more interrogative pitch, like, Such as what?<br /><br />"I dunno. Something pocket-size and innocuous. A pen, maybe?"<br /><br />The sword pulsed, almost like it was laughing. I imagined it saying, A pen sword. That is the stupidest thing I've ever heard.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
